  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c7e26752-655d-4101-a544-b3a9f8ee8751'
      });

  <span id="freeText15654856494915520868" style="display:none">Jody is pretty tough for a sixteen-year-old girl. That's the only reason she's still alive - for now. His friends have left it up to him to find the only living witnesses to their massacre. Or else they'll butcher his family next. But Simon has his own reasons for wanting to get his hands on Jody...</span>

<div id="review_1732542116" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1732542116" />
    <a title="RedemptionDenied" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55677020-redemptiondenied"><img alt="RedemptionDenied" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1732542116?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="RedemptionDenied" class="user" itemprop="url" name="RedemptionDenied" href="/user/show/55677020-redemptiondenied">RedemptionDenied</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55677020-redemptiondenied?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55677020-redemptiondenied?shelf=deranged">deranged</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55677020-redemptiondenied?shelf=gory">gory</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55677020-redemptiondenied?shelf=would-make-a-billy-goat-puke">would-make-a-billy-goat-puke</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55677020-redemptiondenied?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1732542116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11290147454403870427">Well, this was one hell of a twisted story of survival horror, that is filled to the brim with blood, guts and gore. This is my second Laymon novel, so I knew what to expect...sort of. <br/><br/>Sixteen year old, Jody Fargo, is having a 'sleep-over' at her best friends' house - when her friend Evelyn wakes her up; as she believes she's heard a noise downstairs, which sounds like breaking glass. Initially, Jody dismisses that her friend has heard anything - and tries to go back to sleep; and would have if </span>
  <span id="freeText11290147454403870427" style="display:none">Well, this was one hell of a twisted story of survival horror, that is filled to the brim with blood, guts and gore. This is my second Laymon novel, so I knew what to expect...sort of. <br /><br />Sixteen year old, Jody Fargo, is having a 'sleep-over' at her best friends' house - when her friend Evelyn wakes her up; as she believes she's heard a noise downstairs, which sounds like breaking glass. Initially, Jody dismisses that her friend has heard anything - and tries to go back to sleep; and would have if it wasn't for Evelyns persistence. When Evelyn opens her bedroom door though; she ends up getting a spear through her body - and the end of the spear pokes Jody in the naval. Luckily, the perp didn't see her. Once the intruder has gone (with Evelyn still stuck on the end of the spear); Jody makes her way to Andy's room (Evelyns twelve year old brother). He's alive. After giving Andy a heads up; another hostile comes along and enters his room looking for more prey to play with; but Jody's ready, and puts him out of commission by slugging him in the face with a baseball bat. When they get a better look at the dead man; they realise he's wearing another person's butt and legs' over his own naked body. Time to go. <br /><br />As they flee the property; one of the intruders notices them trying to sneak out, and the chase is on. Jody nearly gets apprehended, but just about manages to get away: twice. <br /><br />One of the intruders is abandoned by the gang: which are known as 'The Krulls,' and his name is Simon. He's been designated the job of making sure the two witnesses don't have the opportunity to tattle on them. And if he doesn't take them out, that could have ramifications and not just for him, as the gang have a code to live by: leave no witnesses; never get caught; if it looks like you're going to get captured then you have to go kamikaze, or you and your family will pay. They also torch the properties of victims and remove the bodies, after they've had their fun.<br /><br />The story is told in the first and third person: the first person narrative is basically Simon's confession (insurance policy) on tape, courtesy of Mr &amp; Mrs Weston's cassette recorder. Initially, I was a bit worried with the narrative oscillating every few chapters (as I'm not a fan of first person perspectives) - it worked in this case, though. Actually, I could barely wait for it to switch back to Simon's narrative: which gives an insight into how 'The Krulls' came to be; why they do what they do; what their first kill was like; and of course, we get to know how he plans to track down Jody and Andy - although, he has special plans for Jody. He has the odd practice run with some of his victims; in anticipation of what he is going to do to Jody. <br /><br />The third person narrative is Jody's perspective. Some of the early dialogue is likely to decimate your brain cells, so you need to be careful of that. It seems to get a bit better the further you get into the story - that, or I got used to it. I'm not sure which. Anyway, Jody lives with her father, Jack Fargo (aka - Kong Fargo), and he is a police officer. He has a smirk on his face; courtesy of a .22 bullet passing through his brain. He also walks with a swagger, which looks as if he's walking with an attitude problem: but that's due to a high-speed chase resulting in a collision. He's a lucky guy. He also has a rule of 'having your back to the wall' - which is a trait she has inherited from her father. I think the author had fun making a caricature out of Jack. Some of it was funny, though.<br /><br />Anyway, Jody is a pretty tough character, and its not going to be easy for Simon to get what he wants. <br /><br />As an experiment, I'm tempted to see what happens if I read two Laymon novels' consecutively. Will I go through some kind of metamorphosis, and turn into a cabbage, or a chimp? Don't know.<br /><br />In summation: a really enjoyable survival horror/chase story, that is quite funny at times, despite how descriptive it can be with the rape, blood and gore.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11290147454403870427" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2365671105" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2365671105" />
    <a title="Svetlana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68791366-svetlana"><img alt="Svetlana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1511141526p2/68791366.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2365671105?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Svetlana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Svetlana" href="/user/show/68791366-svetlana">Svetlana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68791366-svetlana?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2365671105" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1742925722195139806">Endless Night started off with a bang and I was instantly hooked. Though I do think I need the Lord’s guidance after finishing it. <br/><br/>Jody was sleeping over at her friend Evelyn’s house when Evelyn heard a crashing sound. Not being able to get it off her mind, they both decided to check the noise out. As soon as she opened the door, Evelyn was speared. Her body leapt straight up and dangled from her doorway. Jody stood frozen behind Evelyn’s limp body, hidden from the killer. She knew she needed to</span>
  <span id="freeText1742925722195139806" style="display:none">Endless Night started off with a bang and I was instantly hooked. Though I do think I need the Lord’s guidance after finishing it. <br /><br />Jody was sleeping over at her friend Evelyn’s house when Evelyn heard a crashing sound. Not being able to get it off her mind, they both decided to check the noise out. As soon as she opened the door, Evelyn was speared. Her body leapt straight up and dangled from her doorway. Jody stood frozen behind Evelyn’s limp body, hidden from the killer. She knew she needed to run, to get away. She managed to find Evelyn’s younger brother Andy alive and they both barely escaped with their lives. There were several killers in the house who had butchered Evelyn’s parents and some of the them started chasing Jody and Andy with axes and sabers. <br /><br />This book really knew how to make me anxious. My heart was in my throat and I was scared about what was to come. Some of the chapters switched to Simon’s POV - one of the killers. I found his chapters incredibly gripping even though they were quite hard to read at times. He narrated all that he and his gang had done in their horrific lives and to their victims. For instance, skinning them and wearing it as clothing. Wtf?? I even gagged at one point lol.<br /><br />I wasn’t very fond of Andy either. I found him to be really annoying and quite perverted for a 12 year old. He didn’t know where to draw the line with Jody, especially when she said no. It was weird, especially considering how his whole family was brutally murdered not long before. Idk.. maybe he wasn’t meant to be a likeable character? <br /><br />Anyways I did enjoy this book and would like to give a shoutout to RedemptionDenied because of who’s review I picked this up. Thanks RD! 😎</span>
  <a data-text-id="1742925722195139806" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8374752571240645391">Laymon novels are a guilty pleasure for me.   <span id="freeText8374752571240645391" style="display:none">Laymon novels are a guilty pleasure for me. They are disgusting and you pretty much have to throw your brains out the window in order to get through them but I have to honestly say they are very much page-turners. If you enjoy senseless murder and mayhem, that is.<br /><br />This one starts out with a sixteen year old girl named Jody sleeping over a friend's house. Innocent enough stuff, until a murderous group of madmen target the home for their next killing spree. Jody survives and manages to escape the home with her friend's younger brother. As they make their escape they are spotted by the murderous louts who slaughtered the family and a chase begins. A chase which encompasses the rest of the book. As expected of a Laymon novel, there is plenty of murder, mayhem, rape and other assorted grossities as well as many plot implausibilities and silly dialogue. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1678020207417868486"><b>4.0 Stars</b><br/>This was one of the most disturbing, terrifying horror novels I have ever read. This one is not for the faint of heart The initial chapters were particularly memorable, launching the reader immediately into the horrifying action. Given the premise, readers must go into this story expecting all the terrible things that could transpire in a home invasion situation.   <span id="freeText1678020207417868486" style="display:none"><b>4.0 Stars</b><br />This was one of the most disturbing, terrifying horror novels I have ever read. This one is not for the faint of heart The initial chapters were particularly memorable, launching the reader immediately into the horrifying action. Given the premise, readers must go into this story expecting all the terrible things that could transpire in a home invasion situation. Trigger warnings for extreme, gruesome violence and sexual assault. This novel will not be for everyone. The writing was not particularly strong, yet I found the plot immersive enough to overlook the weaker aspects of the book.I would recommend this one to experienced (hardened) horror readers who are looking for an intense narrative that might be able to actually scare them.</span>

<div id="review_575919473" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/575919473" />
    <a title="Evans Light" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7008067-evans-light"><img alt="Evans Light" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567305260p2/7008067.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/575919473?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evans Light" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evans Light" href="/user/show/7008067-evans-light">Evans Light</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer575919473" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6512623110359132935">For every Laymon book I find to be perversely delightful, I find another that misses the mark.<br/>Endless Night kicks off with a way-over-the-top opening full of bloody action, but soon after wades into a flabby midsection morass featuring the endless inane family melodrama of individuals who by all rights should be too traumatized to speak.<br/>Jody's friend and her friend's family has been brutally murdered and raped (in that order) in front of her by a pack of crazed maniacs, after which a man dressed</span>
  <span id="freeText6512623110359132935" style="display:none">For every Laymon book I find to be perversely delightful, I find another that misses the mark.<br />Endless Night kicks off with a way-over-the-top opening full of bloody action, but soon after wades into a flabby midsection morass featuring the endless inane family melodrama of individuals who by all rights should be too traumatized to speak.<br />Jody's friend and her friend's family has been brutally murdered and raped (in that order) in front of her by a pack of crazed maniacs, after which a man dressed in corpse flesh chases her through the woods with a machete; yet her biggest concern the following day is whether or not a boy thinks she's cute and hooking her widowed dad up with a single female police officer?<br />Not exactly compelling revenge.<br />Half of the book is written via first person POV of the deranged killer tasked with finishing Jody off, to give the reader more backstory on terrible things that have happened in the past and to make up for the lack of anything remotely exciting happening in the narrative.<br />Laymon does his best to shock the reader, but ultimately it all comes off as more silly than menacing, a MadLibs of disturbing possibilities: <i>Need a wig so your male villain can dress as a woman? Sure! Knock on the nearest random house and scalp the old lady who answers the door. Presto! You're now a glamorous female, able to seduce men with ease. No one will ever tell the difference.</i><br />And so on.<br />Silly is fine when the story is fun (I highly recommend Laymon's Into the Fire or After Midnight as examples of over-the-top perversity done right), but Endless Night ultimately delivers only the "Endless" promised by the title.<br />2.5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6512623110359132935" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_24317225" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/24317225" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1133843-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1367341058p2/1133843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/24317225?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/1133843-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer24317225" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6735330329778371598">This is absolutely the most gruesome, sick, twisted book that I have ever read! It is about a sixteen-year-old girl named Jody who nearly gets slaughtered by a group of killers, the Krulls, while sleeping over at her friend Evelyn's house. Jody manages to escape along with Evelyn's little brother, Andy, while Simon, one of the Krull members, is left behind. Simon's job is to finish off the witnesses or else his girlfriend and his family will be next. Simon becomes obsessed with Jody and can't wa</span>
  <span id="freeText6735330329778371598" style="display:none">This is absolutely the most gruesome, sick, twisted book that I have ever read! It is about a sixteen-year-old girl named Jody who nearly gets slaughtered by a group of killers, the Krulls, while sleeping over at her friend Evelyn's house. Jody manages to escape along with Evelyn's little brother, Andy, while Simon, one of the Krull members, is left behind. Simon's job is to finish off the witnesses or else his girlfriend and his family will be next. Simon becomes obsessed with Jody and can't wait to get to her. I am a big fan of horror novels and this one gave me the chills! It kept my pulse racing, yet I couldn't stop turning the pages, had to find out how it ended. Laymon does not hold back, no lack in details with this one, extremely graphic. If this book were to be made into a movie, I'm not not sure I could stomach watching it, it's that disgusting. If you have a heart condition, do not read this book! It was my first Richard Laymon read, but it definitely won't be the last! </span>
  <a data-text-id="6735330329778371598" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_98670071" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/98670071" />
    <a title="Kasia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2087548-kasia"><img alt="Kasia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494441972p2/2087548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/98670071?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kasia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kasia" href="/user/show/2087548-kasia">Kasia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98670071" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11708553822098838273">I have read over a dozen of Laymon novels and yes by the way I am a fan, when you crave the kind of story that only he writes so well nothing else can satisfy. At least that's how I see it, take a bunch of sympathetic level headed kids, a crazed killer on their tail ( with a very flamboyant but totally cold soul) and you have some page gripping moments, you'd want to read this over the weekend if you have some time to put into this, it's an entertaining ride and it's well embellished for those w</span>
  <span id="freeText11708553822098838273" style="display:none">I have read over a dozen of Laymon novels and yes by the way I am a fan, when you crave the kind of story that only he writes so well nothing else can satisfy. At least that's how I see it, take a bunch of sympathetic level headed kids, a crazed killer on their tail ( with a very flamboyant but totally cold soul) and you have some page gripping moments, you'd want to read this over the weekend if you have some time to put into this, it's an entertaining ride and it's well embellished for those who like some icky moments. Once again Laymon proves that his well used formula of bad men after pretty girls works to grip the reader, Jody is on a sleepover at a friend's house when noise wakes her up, what happens next is the appetizer of the story which sets up the tone and the urgency for the reminder of the novel, there is no time to breathe nor relax when this wild ride starts, and get used to creepy, crazy and nasty it can appear at any time in Laymon's world. I miss you man, wish you were still around to churn out some more...<br /><br />This story line echoed a bit of Dean Koontz's "Intensity" which was an amazing book, a must read for horror fans, it has that nasty surprise of being in the wrong place at the wrong time but take to another level, you're at your friends house at a sleepover and her whole family except for one boy gets hacked to pieces, talk about picking the wrong night and what it will take to keep your precious life!<br /><br />Jody manages to escape through some well written pages - I was pulling the paper to the point of breakage, but what waits for her next isn't any easier. One person in particular from the bunch of mysterious killers is on her trail, not only is he meant to kill and silence her but he's smitten with her as well, talk about double lousy luck! There are many unlucky houses that he uses to hide in or use something from, and those descriptions were the most interesting in the book because he gets quite creative with all that he finds in each house, the residents included - nothing is wasted, scalps included... but overall the whole story had a quick and crazy pace, there is no rest until the last page. I'm happy that the ending was pretty shocking, it was explosive until the last letter and period sign and sometimes I read an amazing and suspenseful book where the bad buy gets a buh-bye in a page or two after hours of torment, that to me is almost a cop out, this guarantees a satisfying finish, good or bad you judge but it was a great weekend read for those who like a crazy horror book or those who are Laymon fans, enjoy!<br /><br />- Kasia S. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11708553822098838273" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159370326" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4372165385280070152">I have to say I was disappointed reading "Body Rides" with Laymon. I mean, I had heard he was the greatest thing this side of horror, but just wasn’t feeling it. After reading "Endless Nights," however, I just might jump on the Laymon happy go lucky bandwagon after all!<br/><br/>The book starts off with horror and ends with even worse horror.   <span id="freeText4372165385280070152" style="display:none">I have to say I was disappointed reading "Body Rides" with Laymon. I mean, I had heard he was the greatest thing this side of horror, but just wasn’t feeling it. After reading "Endless Nights," however, I just might jump on the Laymon happy go lucky bandwagon after all!<br /><br />The book starts off with horror and ends with even worse horror. From the very first few pages, tension is high enough to induce a nervous breakdown in the reader.<br /><br />Laymon whips up a dessert full of dark atmosphere, rich characters, smooth pacing, and mouth- watering suspense. This book is a little long when you look at it from a side view, but when you're reading it, you'd never notice the length because you're so preoccupied with what you're reading. Most of the pages are blood-soaked; Laymon doesn't hesitate to describe the violence and horrible happenings in gruesome, unflinching detail.<br /><br />If you want to jump into Laymon, make Endless Night your intended spot. Read it once, read it again, and then lock it away for safe keeping! </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1979172910" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6715867325663552845">3.5 - 3.75 stars. <br/><br/>I wasn't expecting THAT much from this, so I can't really say that I was disappointed. <br/><br/>The first thing that comes to my mind when I think about this book is <b>gross</b>. Laymon's writing brought everything that happened in this book to life, and sometimes I had to put the book down because I needed a break from time to time. <br/><br/>This book is told in two points of views, Jody and Simon. This is an interesting contrast because Jody is a seemingly squeaky clean 16 year old girl, and Simon i</span>
  <span id="freeText6715867325663552845" style="display:none">3.5 - 3.75 stars. <br /><br />I wasn't expecting THAT much from this, so I can't really say that I was disappointed. <br /><br />The first thing that comes to my mind when I think about this book is <b>gross</b>. Laymon's writing brought everything that happened in this book to life, and sometimes I had to put the book down because I needed a break from time to time. <br /><br />This book is told in two points of views, Jody and Simon. This is an interesting contrast because Jody is a seemingly squeaky clean 16 year old girl, and Simon is the complete opposite - he's a serial killer - oh, yeah, he's also a rapist. <br /><br />I haven't really ever read a book that it was told in the point of view of both the killer who's hunting someone down, as well as the hunted, and I thought that it worked great because it allowed the reader to see both sides of the spectrum. <br /><br />One of my biggest qualms with this book was the <b> writing </b>. IT WAS SO FREAKING BAD OMG! I was constantly rolling my eyes as I was reading because it literally read like a lifetime or Hallmark script. <br /><br />Overall, I really enjoyed this one, but the kind of terrible writing took off a few stars from me, but it was a pretty fun read, which was exactly what I was looking for.</span>

<div id="review_902820964" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/902820964" />
    <a title="Stuart Keane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29924908-stuart-keane"><img alt="Stuart Keane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510580178p2/29924908.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/902820964?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stuart Keane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stuart Keane" href="/user/show/29924908-stuart-keane">Stuart Keane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29924908-stuart-keane?shelf=must-read-horror">must-read-horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer902820964" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9786013389598396850">I discovered Richard Laymon at a very young age. Once hooked, I grabbed any novel I could get my horror-seeking little hands on. I've read all but two of Laymon's works but this is the one that will always resonate with me. To this day, this still stands at #2 on my Favourite Laymon list.<br/><br/>Laymon really pulls out the stops in this book. At times, it feels like a Hollywood blockbuster and a gritty independent project combined. Every scene is easily imaginable due to Laymon's tempered pace, vivid im</span>
  <span id="freeText9786013389598396850" style="display:none">I discovered Richard Laymon at a very young age. Once hooked, I grabbed any novel I could get my horror-seeking little hands on. I've read all but two of Laymon's works but this is the one that will always resonate with me. To this day, this still stands at #2 on my Favourite Laymon list.<br /><br />Laymon really pulls out the stops in this book. At times, it feels like a Hollywood blockbuster and a gritty independent project combined. Every scene is easily imaginable due to Laymon's tempered pace, vivid imagery and realistic characters. The less experienced horror fan will put this down after a few chapters but for those who love their horror lurid, gory and extremely violent will jump in head-first. You'll also be treated to possibly the worst enemy in the Laymon back catalogue...you won't be disappointed. <br /><br />A tale told from first-person and third-person, he flits effortlessly between the two perspectives and creates a genuine, pulse-pounding tension that even the hardest horror fan (me included) will find hard to forget. As the book sprints to it's unpredictable conclusion, you'd be forgiven for getting caught up in the story, the mystery and the graphic crimes that take place within. I still flinch when <i>that</i> axe smashes the patio doors...<br /><br />Five stars then. Simply, and deservedly, because this book really tuned me into adult horror. Flesh by Laymon may have been my debut to adult horror but Endless Night was my encore. A great, gory, horrific read.<br /><br /> <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9786013389598396850" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2784359752" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16005685182384565464">Endless Night is a tight coil of tension overflowing with unspeakable horrors and acts of human depravity which will churn the stomachs of even the most horror-hardened of readers. <br/><br/>Jody and Andy, two teens find themselves in the cross-hairs of a cult of crazies hellbent on murder most macabre. Lucky for Jody, her father is a police chief, unlucky for her, is one of the cult crazies has an unhealthy obsession with her, one which her father may not be able to shield her from. <br/><br/>I couldn't read this </span>
  <span id="freeText16005685182384565464" style="display:none">Endless Night is a tight coil of tension overflowing with unspeakable horrors and acts of human depravity which will churn the stomachs of even the most horror-hardened of readers. <br /><br />Jody and Andy, two teens find themselves in the cross-hairs of a cult of crazies hellbent on murder most macabre. Lucky for Jody, her father is a police chief, unlucky for her, is one of the cult crazies has an unhealthy obsession with her, one which her father may not be able to shield her from. <br /><br />I couldn't read this book fast enough. Jody and Andy are characters you want to care for, while the cult are brutal and relentless which creates a nice yin to the innocent yang of the prey.<br /><br />My rating: 5/5 stars. This was my first introduction to Richard Laymon's work and I can't wait to read more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16005685182384565464" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2407793535" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2407793535" />
    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2155899-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499481703p2/2155899.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2407793535?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/2155899-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/38236662-endless-night">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2155899-michelle?shelf=edit-fail">edit-fail</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2155899-michelle?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2155899-michelle?shelf=guns">guns</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2155899-michelle?shelf=misogyny">misogyny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2155899-michelle?shelf=awesome-title">awesome-title</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2155899-michelle?shelf=dead-pet-horror-or-thriller-cliche">dead-pet-horror-or-thriller-cliche</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2155899-michelle?shelf=rape-culture">rape-culture</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2155899-michelle?shelf=too-creepy-to-be-sexy">too-creepy-to-be-sexy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2155899-michelle?shelf=80s">80s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2155899-michelle?shelf=outdated">outdated</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2407793535" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18409397850998315134">My mind is a-whir with all the points I want to make here, and all the disclaimers I have as well. Ultimately, this book is dated, which means some of the issues I have are a result of societal evolution. Still, my making allowances for this, as I routinely do, did not help me to enjoy this book more. <br/><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1532632016i/26033535.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Before I get into the main focus of my issues -- but the image above is a preview -- I'd like to say almost nothing worked for me in the story. I found all the characters either creepy or strange</span>
  <span id="freeText18409397850998315134" style="display:none">My mind is a-whir with all the points I want to make here, and all the disclaimers I have as well. Ultimately, this book is dated, which means some of the issues I have are a result of societal evolution. Still, my making allowances for this, as I routinely do, did not help me to enjoy this book more. <br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1532632016i/26033535.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Before I get into the main focus of my issues -- but the image above is a preview -- I'd like to say almost nothing worked for me in the story. I found all the characters either creepy or strange in their reactions, down to choices and to dialogue. There is a character that is supposed to be a creepy relative, and he was only slightly more off than anyone else. The good guys and the bad guy seemed to be a bit similar. <br><br>The Kindle edition I read is also very poorly done, filled with formatting issues. <br><br>Anyhow, there are 2 POV characters, one a 16-year-old girl with a sexually predatory murderer on her trail, and the other is the sexually predatory murderer. Fair enough when stated that way. <br><br>Jody, the girl, spends the majority of the book in night shirts or missing her pants. She has a short night shirt, she has a short and tight night shirt, and she has a loose night shirt that -- oopsies -- falls off her shoulders and allows people to see down it. <br><br>Her narration is obsessed with what her night shirts are doing at any given moment, what the hem line is doing, what parts of her body are being revealed. The thinness of the material. Even when she is being chased, she is conscious of these details. At one point, she is wearing shorts, but sustains an injury high on the thigh, and so off with the shorts. <br><br>She also takes a really long shower at one point in which she thinks of the boy she likes. It doesn't completely go masturbatory on her part, but the whole thing seems designed with the intent of the rest of her narration -- to remind us she is an attractive (but in many ways innocent and untouched) 16 year old. <br><br>I don't think Laymon is trying to say this girl is obsessed with her own body, but I think he is obsessed with her body, and doing the thing some male authors do of thinking women are constantly in thought and deed catering to the male libido. He isn't in her head so much as watching her and making his fixations her thoughts. <br><br>Which the other POV character -- the sexually predatory murderer -- is going to cover just fine. He has a purpose in being obsessed with her body and her, er, sexy innocence. Her POV should be a reprieve from that, even a rebuke of that as we know her as a full human being. In that way, authors get their cake and etcetera, etcetera. They can be creepy and empathetic, and you can't extrapolate what messed up thoughts they share with the bad guy. <br><br>But everyone is obsessed all the time with the female body. <br><br>There's a 12 year old boy who has his whole family slaughtered -- first couple chapters -- but never loses his fascination with copping a feel or catching a glimpse of Jody or a female cop character. I'll return to the female cop character.<br><br>This kid is just creepy, and combined with everything and everyone else, seems to imply all men are capable of assaults on women they deem attractive. Or people? There are a couple sexually predatory murderers mentioned who like boys. <br><br>The kid's erection becomes a plot point. There are moments when Jody also seems to give in a little to his advances. She says he's like a creepy little brother, but she also lets him stick his nose in her crotch for comfort -- not making that up -- or kisses him on the mouth since he's upset. She's worried her father might come in and get the wrong idea. <br><br>Jody packs at one point to leave to evade the bad guy, and she thinks her father will be upset that she didn't pack a skirt or dress, not that there are any plans to go anywhere that would specifically need those items, just that it's somehow wrong for her not to have access to these items. The bad guy on more than one occasion wonders why women don't wear skirts and dresses anymore since pants and culottes impede access to ... stuff. <br><br>With the exception of an old woman, I do believe every other female given a name is sexualized to some extent. The only other female character of any note, other than victims of the central gang, is a female police officer. Upon meeting Jody, she helps bandage her upper thigh injury -- the one that forces Jody to remove her shorts -- and Jody makes note of seeing down the woman's blouse, and reveals the cop has a thing for black sexy lingerie. <br><br>God, what's her name? Bonnie, I think. We'll roll with it. <br><br>Like Jody, Bonnie's character is mostly a hot body in revealing clothes, with just a subtle whiff of actual characterization that is not about her hot body. Jody and Bonnie are both good with guns and fighters, which I still think is presented as being hot. <br><br>Jody's father makes clear he is attracted to Bonnie, and Jody understands it since Bonnie has big breasts that bounce when she shoots a gun. <br><br><i>Dad wasn’t watching the target. His eyes were on Sharon. Jody checked; that’s where Andy was staring, too. Watching her there, NRA cap turned backward so its bill stuck out behind her, the rifle jumping with each shot and throwing out flashes of brass as its muzzle spat fire and white smoke, her whole body absorbing the recoils that hit her with quick hard jolts and shook her shirt and made her thighs vibrate even though Jody knew her legs must be almost as solid as wood. She does look great, Jody thought. No wonder the guys are staring like a couple of nuts. They’re probably wishing they were on the other side so they could watch what the recoils are doing to her boobs.</i><br><br>Oh, Sharon. Bonnie is Sharon. <br><br>Sharbonnie has packed -- for the trip that is off-duty, but not unrelated to her job -- a flimsy robe. In case anyone is wondering, she shares with the 12-year-old erection and Jody's dad (and Jody) she is naked under the robe, and let's head to the vending machine. She also shares over lunch that she has a tattoo in a mystery location. <br><br>Because ever and always, the author wants to make sure the reader has something about the bodies of his female caricatures, er, characters, to imagine. <br><br>Jody's father, btw, has "had kept his chivalry in spite of feminism," and specifically worries that the condom will fall off inside Jody if she sleeps with a boy. Not just general failure rate of condoms so much as wanting to mention specifically what might happen if someone is INSIDE his daughter. His daughter who should wear dresses and skirts more. He slapped her on the rear once, which is not in isolation a problem for me. It just happens to be partnered with everything else. A whole lot of night shirts and testosterone. <br><br>Which reminds me that Jody has no connection to any other female character, other than the big-boobed cop. She starts the book with a friend who doesn't make it to page 10, I don't think. No other friends that I recall are mentioned, or call her to see how she's doing. No friend she wishes to call and talk about the friend they just lost. Her mother is dead. Her world is entirely males who objectify females or one female written to be objectified. There is a love interest who has no substance, maybe because Laymon realized the limits to how many people Jody actually seemed to know. <br><br>I like good, twisted villains. I do. But I'm wired to care about Jody, maybe even more in this case than the author cares about Jody. And I'm of an age where it irritates me that she is spends the book as T and A. That even that strong, capable part of her -- or Sharbonnie's -- nature seems to be given as just another reason she is sexy and pursued by the bad guy. <br><br>I read this, and I feel both like Jody and Jody's mom, which makes me feel so sad to see her portrayal. And I realize how spoiled I've become as women authors get a voice, and many male authors are writing women with more empathy and complexity. <br><br>Endless Night is the book version of slasher films. Jody is a final girl. 1980s me, coming of age, wouldn't know to be sad or offended. The author clearly wasn't aiming to be a sexist. Jody is scrappy, after all, which is why the bad guy -- Simon -- can't leave her alone. <br><br><i>It’s more than just how she looks. She has ... a quality. A freshness. Maybe it also has to do partly with how spunky she was when we were after her.</i><br><br>Anyhow, Simon's POV is super gross, but I think it should be. The author really pushes the envelope with describing Simon and his cohorts raping and torturing people. And I get it -- horror novel, not Sunday brunch -- but my issues with the Jody POV make me unable to go along. Because there are similarities, right? Everybody objectifies women, even the good guys. <br><br>Simon, hand to God, even objectifies himself as he spends a lot of the novel disguised as a woman. I can't even untangle this plot point. Is the author saying Simon's enjoyment of dressing this way cements him as a sick puppy? Is (was, sorry) the author incapable of writing someone dressed this way, and describing one's self, without making it about level of attractiveness? <br><br>Oh, look, the male villain put on a dress and now he's breasting boobily too. I mean, how could one not? ;)<br><br>Anyhow, there were moments of horror and suspense. Those happened. This is why I upgraded to 2 stars. But I never want to read a Laymon book again. I have better choices in horror, in authors, in life, than to read books that gross me out in a bad way. And I know you know there are good gross outs and bad ones. <br><br>It's not Laymon's fault that time has moved on. That's what time does. It's not his fault that we live in a time with increasing book options. It's not his fault that many female readers expect a different portrayal of female characters that aren't about how many boners they cause, and even when they are cognizant of that, they're also quite possibly addressing and critiquing that. <br><br>Anyhow, a recent horror novel I really enjoyed was:<br><br> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40530821.Violets_are_Red" title="Violets are Red by Mylo Carbia" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1529021360s/40530821.jpg" alt="Violets are Red by Mylo Carbia" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But if you think you'll enjoy Endless Night, have at it. I just couldn't stop thinking, "Oh, THIS is what people mean when they say torture porn." </span>
  <a data-text-id="18409397850998315134" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer461976639" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11244271694676641548">This was one of the better Laymon books I have read lately. I was happy to find that Laymon went all out as he usually does, but there was a story to go along with it. The last couple of his I read were disappointing. Endless Night features one of the most vile, perverted and absolutely evil antagonists I can remember reading in quite some time.<br/>The good guys were pretty likeable with the exception of Andy. I just wasn't too keen on his character, and some of the situations involving him seemed r</span>
  <span id="freeText11244271694676641548" style="display:none">This was one of the better Laymon books I have read lately. I was happy to find that Laymon went all out as he usually does, but there was a story to go along with it. The last couple of his I read were disappointing. Endless Night features one of the most vile, perverted and absolutely evil antagonists I can remember reading in quite some time.<br />The good guys were pretty likeable with the exception of Andy. I just wasn't too keen on his character, and some of the situations involving him seemed ridiculous and unnecessary to the story.<br />Laymon has a way of taking little side-trips in some of his novels, okay quite a few of them actually, but the one in this book was nowhere near as long and boring as some of the others. The only reason I didn't give this one five stars was because I thought the sections about Jody and Andy were pretty dry and sometimes rather pointless, while the strong segments were all the ones narrated by Simon Quirt. I don't know what kind of person I am for enjoying a serial butcher telling his story better, but there you have it. Laymon just wrote those passages with much more enthusiasm.<br />There were also a lot o puns and word play in this book. e.g. the villain's name. (S. Quirt)... you'll get that one if you read it.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13048799096789410521">I'll admit that part 1 had my full attention. The disgust became too much to ignore after the escape. All was downhill once Simon's POV came into play.<br/>This is a sick read. Foul. I never hated any book so much since I read James Patterson's vomit-inducing Swimsuit.   <span id="freeText13048799096789410521" style="display:none">I'll admit that part 1 had my full attention. The disgust became too much to ignore after the escape. All was downhill once Simon's POV came into play.<br />This is a sick read. Foul. I never hated any book so much since I read James Patterson's vomit-inducing Swimsuit. I have yet to read another Patterson novel since, and I won't even look once at another Laymon book.<br />I was quite turned off by all the graphic rape talk and the way he wrote sexually about Andy. Andy was 12 years old for gripe's sake. That kind of stuff should be saved for at least 17 if it needs to be written at all. I don't want to read about a 12 year old boy and his erection while watching a serial killer-rapist lick the "crack" of a girl Andy is supposed to feel brotherly towards. <br />No thank you.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer950362326138367700">...this here's my friend, Richard. He's kinda shy. Won't come in for a soda, or tea or anything like that.   <span id="freeText950362326138367700" style="display:none">...this here's my friend, Richard. He's kinda shy. Won't come in for a soda, or tea or anything like that. Just sort of run into him when I take my trash outside. He's sometimes just standing there, and he'll turn to me, almost as if he's been talking to somebody else and just stops mid sentence. But I never see no one. My wife's a little spooked by him. She says she's glad he won't come in. Might scare the babies. Or the dogs. Well, he ain't a bad guy in my humble opinion. Says he works third shift at the Sunoco, and writes a little in his spare time. He wrote this here yarn called 'Endless Night'. Although the story takes place over several endless nights. But hey, who's countin', right? It's the fourth story I've read by Richard, and I've gotta say, it ain't his best. It's more for the folks who like a little a shot of psycho juice from the freak-jug. Ain't nothing wrong with that. And the psycho he writes about in this one does have a good dose of charisma. But me, well, I just like it when Richard tells a good old fashioned spine tingler, with a few surprises thrown in. Like a bike hag. Or a dreadlocked troll guy. Or a freakish clown standing alone in a dark room full of clown memorabilia. Yeah, I don't need a whole lot to get a chuckle, and that sweaty, sleazy feeling. But ol Richard, boy he always comes through with a good little morsel of piss yer britches frightfulness. </span>

The great thing about <i>this</i> Richard Laymon novel is it was smart. The violence was necessary to the killer's motivation and the victim's demise. Sometimes in horror where the violence is senseless it just irritates me. <br/><br/>Simon Quist is the murderer and you are told this early and let known his background and understand why he is the way he is.   <span id="freeText11296847965213298105" style="display:none">Jody is at a sleepover when something wakes her up. Going to investigate starts the ENDLESS NIGHT. The great thing about <i>this</i> Richard Laymon novel is it was smart. The violence was necessary to the killer's motivation and the victim's demise. Sometimes in horror where the violence is senseless it just irritates me. <br /><br />Simon Quist is the murderer and you are told this early and let known his background and understand why he is the way he is. Wouldn't it be nice to know, that while still twisted and sick, why a killer enjoys torturing and killing? I think for what is was worth it gave me a better understanding for the violence and why Simon felt he had to do what he was doing. <br /><br />What I had heard about Richard Laymon being a great horror novelist proved true in this first novel I had ever read by him. Not to heavy but just intense enough for you need a cleansing breath at the end.</span>

<div id="review_3559452414" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3559452414" />
    <a title="Phil" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/76396700-phil"><img alt="Phil" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516033071p2/76396700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3559452414?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phil" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phil" href="/user/show/76396700-phil">Phil</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76396700-phil?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76396700-phil?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3559452414" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8655713649852149107">Not quite sure what to make of Endless Night, but it definitely has Laymon's trademark juvenile sexism and gore stamped on it. Our main POV and protagonist Jody is 16 and the daughter of a cop in LA. The book starts off with her at a sleepover at her BFF's house, when a group of men dressed in human skin and covered in stinking dead person slime, armed with axes, spears and what not, break in and slaughter her BFF's family. Jody manages to escape the house with her BFF's 12 year old brother. We </span>
  <span id="freeText8655713649852149107" style="display:none">Not quite sure what to make of Endless Night, but it definitely has Laymon's trademark juvenile sexism and gore stamped on it. Our main POV and protagonist Jody is 16 and the daughter of a cop in LA. The book starts off with her at a sleepover at her BFF's house, when a group of men dressed in human skin and covered in stinking dead person slime, armed with axes, spears and what not, break in and slaughter her BFF's family. Jody manages to escape the house with her BFF's 12 year old brother. We then switch to the POV of Simon, one of the homicidal sociopaths who attacked the house, who was left behind to finish off the witnesses. The novel oscillates between Jody and Simon thereafter, keeping us abreast of Jody and Simon's plans to get her.<br /><br />There are some interesting things in the novel, such as Simon's 'confessions' so to speak as he gradually gives his backstory to a tape recorder during his pursuit of Jody. The story of how his group of 'friends' became ruthless killers in their young teens and evolved to their current status of homicidal maniacs who randomly choose houses at night to begin their 'games' so to speak. Truly nasty stuff from Laymon! And yes, he does manage to build some good tension, especially at the start and the end. <br /><br />Nonetheless, Endless Night did not really provide much emotional investment. Andy, the rescued brother of Jody's BFF, is a typical Laymon pervert obsessed with Jody's body, and of course, we have endless descriptions of her breasts and various outfits. Jody is a strong protagonist, but she simply rolls with the punches throughout the novel. Unless you really enjoy reading about rapey sociopaths, and how they get turned on during their escapades, I would give this a pass. 2.5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8655713649852149107" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2400081919" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2400081919" />
    <a title="Sarah Marie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6515737-sarah-marie"><img alt="Sarah Marie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589089368p2/6515737.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2400081919?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Marie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Marie" href="/user/show/6515737-sarah-marie">Sarah Marie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/38236662-endless-night">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6515737-sarah-marie?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6515737-sarah-marie?shelf=holding-me-hostage">holding-me-hostage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6515737-sarah-marie?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6515737-sarah-marie?shelf=standalones">standalones</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6515737-sarah-marie?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6515737-sarah-marie?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6515737-sarah-marie?shelf=booktube-made-me-do-it">booktube-made-me-do-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6515737-sarah-marie?shelf=on-my-kindle">on-my-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6515737-sarah-marie?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6515737-sarah-marie?shelf=some-people-die">some-people-die</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2400081919" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9897031599238630971"><u>Endless Night</u> by Richard Laymon<br/><br/><b>1 star</b><br/><br/><p>Jody is sleeping over at her best friend Evelyn’s house when Evelyn shakes her awake in the dead of night and claims that a window downstairs has been broken. As Evelyn and Jody brave waking up the parents in the house Evelyn is murdered with a spear. The killer walks off with her body and Jody is able to find a weapon and get Jody’s brother. There’s something strange about the killer in the house. There’s more than one, they smell rotten, don’t appear to be </p></span>
  <span id="freeText9897031599238630971" style="display:none"><u>Endless Night</u> by Richard Laymon<br /><br /><b>1 star</b><br /><br /><p>Jody is sleeping over at her best friend Evelyn’s house when Evelyn shakes her awake in the dead of night and claims that a window downstairs has been broken. As Evelyn and Jody brave waking up the parents in the house Evelyn is murdered with a spear. The killer walks off with her body and Jody is able to find a weapon and get Jody’s brother. There’s something strange about the killer in the house. There’s more than one, they smell rotten, don’t appear to be wearing clothes—that is until one sees that they are adorned in human flesh, and seem to be partaking in the eating of Evelyn’s parents. Jody and Andy barely escape. Simon’s gang of ruthless killers have left him behind because no witnesses can be left behind. He failed at capturing Jody and Andy and now he must capture them and make sure they can’t reveal any more secrets. Armed with a tape recorder, a plan for destruction, and a thirst for the inhumane torture of Jody and anyone who stands in his way of getting his hands on her. I read this book for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/582055-peter-s-book-club" rel="nofollow noopener">Peter’s Book Club</a>! I love Peter and I trust his recommendations. I’ve read so many books that are favorites that he has recommended, but not every book one picks up from someone’s recommendation will be one you walk away loving. In fact, Endless Night by Richard Laymon may be one of my most hated reads ever. I’ll just be up front, Laymon can create a fast-paced narrative that is easy to fly through, but the content left my stomach in knots. I like dark novels. I read and watch true crime, my favorite author is Stephen King, and I’ve done maybe a little too much research into serial killers. I like the macabre, but this isn’t macabre this is obscene. This is a complete degradation and glorification of rape, torture, and murder. I was expecting that, but Laymon writes in such a way that it feels almost like he wants you to root for Simon and agree with him as he is scalping a woman he just murdered, stuffing her in a freezer, and then putting her hair on his head as a wig. No thanks. I don’t want to sympathize, understand, or root for anyone like that. I like reading about the depraved, but not when it feels like I’m reading a book that could potentially inspire other readers to carry out violent acts. Let’s not forget that the writing is just bad. Grammar errors aside and the constant annoyance of the letter I being written as the number 1, Laymon is not a crafter of a beautiful sentence. His diction choice is subpar and its obvious he uses words for dramatic effect instead of to get one thinking.</p><br /><br /><b>Whimsical Writing Scale: 1</b><br /><br /><p>Jody, our heroine, and the girl who everyone tells, <i>“You don’t look too bad for a young lady who’s just been shot up,”</i> (real quote folks on page 169) and happens to be the luckiest survivor in the history of survivors. She happens to be well-trained in guns and self-defense, which makes for a thrilling opening sequence with her bashing heads and surviving, but beyond that she is as bland as unbuttered toast. I can’t tell you one thing I liked about her because I didn’t.</p><br /><br /><b>Kick-Butt Heroine Scale: 1</b><br /><br /><p>Then there’s Andy, the twelve-year-old brother of her best friend. Andy reminds me of that disgusting little psychopath from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4945931.Apt_Pupil_A_Novella_in_Different_Seasons" title="Apt Pupil A Novella in Different Seasons by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Apt Pupil: A Novella in Different Seasons</a> by Stephen King (now that’s a fantastic character study on psychopaths done right) who was obsessed with WWII and concentration camps. Andy even reminiscence about pictures he saw of human lampshades even though his family was just brutally murdered by a murder cult clothed in human skin. LIKE WHAT. Then <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[he watches Jody almost be sexually assaulted and doesn’t immediately shoot Simon on the spot. He watches and allows Simon to manipulate and taunt him because wow a hot naked chick. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I just can’t fathom who would actually act this way and I can’t help but wonder if Laymon depicted Andy this way because he was planning to keep him alive and have him become a twisted killer with Simon. Jody’s father and the cop, Sharon, are the only characters in this novel who don’t seem to have a thirst for degrading their fellow human aside from Jody. This book is just a ball of sunshine when it comes to portraying humans loving one another and not wanting to run them over with cars.</p><br /><br /><b>Character Scale: 1</b><br /><br /><p><b>The Villain-</b> Why did we need to hear from Simon? This book could’ve been two hundred pages shorter and far less disgusting. I couldn’t stand being inside his head (technically voice recording) and it made my skin crawl. I wasn’t the only one in the book club either with this problem. It was too much. He’s a scary human, but a good villain? Honestly, no. The reason these perverts starting killing and torturing humans is disgusting and also nearly implausible with human psychology. I’m just thankful that I will never be inside his head again.</p><br /><br /><b>Villain Scale: 1</b><br /><br /><p>Will I read another Richard Laymon? Highly unlikely. He’s just not for me. However, I’m not against it, but I’m not jumping for joy thinking about the prospect of reading another twisted narrative. I think I’m better off sticking with Stephen King, Karin Slaughter, and Gillian Flynn when it comes to character studies of the depraved and sick. I’m going to take a hard pass. However, I’m happy that I read this alongside the people in Peter’s Book Club because I love Peter and he talks about Laymon all the time. It was nice to finally pick up an author he praises often who isn’t more recent. Would I recommend this? Ere on the side of caution. I never will tell someone not to read a book because books change lives, but I don’t think anyone’s life will be changed for the better with picking this one up. Go read Apt Pupil instead.</p><br /><br /><b>Plotastic Scale: 1<br /><br />Cover Thoughts: Spooky creepy horror cover. It has that old school mass market paperback vibe.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="9897031599238630971" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_125106709" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/125106709" />
    <a title="Kelly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1347210-kelly"><img alt="Kelly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310833806p2/1347210.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/125106709?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly" href="/user/show/1347210-kelly">Kelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1347210-kelly?shelf=beach-book">beach-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1347210-kelly?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1347210-kelly?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125106709" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11814826949466680752">Warning: For all of you who are weak of heart, loose of mind or those that hold a moral stance equal to or greater than Tammy Faye Baker - need turn away! For the love of all that’s innocent and pure, turn away! <br/> <br/>Now, for all you morally lacking readers out there who thrive on violence, gore and degradation of the lowest kind or just aren’t the sharpest pencil in the box, I have one word for you – Sweet! With no holds barred, Laymon gives us a tale so chilling and boundless that you begin to wan</span>
  <span id="freeText11814826949466680752" style="display:none">Warning: For all of you who are weak of heart, loose of mind or those that hold a moral stance equal to or greater than Tammy Faye Baker - need turn away! For the love of all that’s innocent and pure, turn away! <br /> <br />Now, for all you morally lacking readers out there who thrive on violence, gore and degradation of the lowest kind or just aren’t the sharpest pencil in the box, I have one word for you – Sweet! With no holds barred, Laymon gives us a tale so chilling and boundless that you begin to wander if the man slept a wink … ever! <br /> <br />While the plot is not all that original, the execution of it is. Instead of giving you the option of dipping your toes in to test the water, Laymon throws you headfirst into a passage of unimaginable terror. Between the blood that was shed, the panic of what was to happen next and the nonchalance of the depravity shown I was almost ready to revisit my lunch. The man is my Hero! The pace in the book is hypersonic. From the first page to the last the action is non-stop, never leaving room for doubts or reflection. <br /> <br />The atmosphere is heavy with pressure and tension. As you begin to immerse yourself in the book, you feel the weight of time running out and the build-up rising. For this I suggest a nice cup of chamomile afterwards because I guarantee you will feel like jumping out of your skin from the compression. Well developed and three dimensional, the characters were completely plausible. The players evoke an intimate familiarity, giving you the illusion that they could be anyone, everyone or maybe someone quite close to you. <br /> <br />The style of writing is up front and honest. Laymon intends to make you as uncomfortable as he can while instilling fear at every opportunity. Switching views throughout between Jody and Simon, the author weaves a tale of nail-biting suspense that keeps the reader interested to find out what happens next. The man is a sadistic genius! <br /> <br />My rating? I give it a 5. Put on those shoes, grab the keys and go buy this book new, Now! <br /><br />-As reviewed for Horror-Web.com</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4814027230563524940">Dick Laymon comes through again with the cheap thrills. This time it's kind of a family vacay meets psycho bloopers blend of shock shtick. I think this one is one of his best, although I've only read about 7 or 8 of his books.<br/><br/>I won't run over the plot with you too much but I will say that this book has a split personality and I really enjoyed that aspect. It is told in third person when concerning our damsel in distress, but when the perspective switches over to the big baddie, it is told in fir</span>
  <span id="freeText4814027230563524940" style="display:none">Dick Laymon comes through again with the cheap thrills. This time it's kind of a family vacay meets psycho bloopers blend of shock shtick. I think this one is one of his best, although I've only read about 7 or 8 of his books.<br /><br />I won't run over the plot with you too much but I will say that this book has a split personality and I really enjoyed that aspect. It is told in third person when concerning our damsel in distress, but when the perspective switches over to the big baddie, it is told in first person. The parts of the book told in first person, by Mr. Simon "Nair Legs" Quirt, are by far the most entertaining parts of the tale. The misadventures of this psycho-killer are hilarious. He hates dogs, loves cross-dressing, and has a "never give up" attitude that makes him, and the book, a real winner.<br /><br />Richard Laymon is fucked up. This we know. In this book you will read as he describes sexy scenes involving a twelve year old boy, brings back the fun of scalping people, and shows us that the scariest thing for the Bogeyman is actually a little, gay dog. If you are into this type of thing, just read the book and you will surely get your jollies like I did. And like Richard did. </span>

<div id="review_53261243" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/53261243" />
    <a title="kas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2118293-kas"><img alt="kas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1240178677p2/2118293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/53261243?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="kas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="kas" href="/user/show/2118293-kas">kas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">violent-sex horror enthusiasts</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer53261243" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5784849153664217228">If you like violent-sex horror, you will love this. <br/><br/>The book was a quick read that really kept me on the edge of my seat. I am not a quick reader (verrrry slow) and read this pretty quickly. <br/><br/>Overview:<br/>Basically it is told from two points of view from one of the survivors and one of the killers.<br/><br/>Jody, a young girl staying at a friends house, wakes up to her friends concern of someone in the house and quickly sees her friend killed. She and the friends brother survive and are soon chased by the kill</span>
  <span id="freeText5784849153664217228" style="display:none">If you like violent-sex horror, you will love this. <br /><br />The book was a quick read that really kept me on the edge of my seat. I am not a quick reader (verrrry slow) and read this pretty quickly. <br /><br />Overview:<br />Basically it is told from two points of view from one of the survivors and one of the killers.<br /><br />Jody, a young girl staying at a friends house, wakes up to her friends concern of someone in the house and quickly sees her friend killed. She and the friends brother survive and are soon chased by the killers.<br /><br />They get away and one of the killers, Simon, is left behind to retrieve the kids. <br /><br />The books has many creepy/disgusting moments that keep you interested. There are some (few) slower moments, I found kinda boring, but I was so involved, I barely noticed. <br /><br />After reading The Woods are Dark, I became a Laymon fan, but after this book, I AM A LAYMON FAN :) </span>
  <a data-text-id="5784849153664217228" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
